Free Talk

On Treating Headaches by Curing Feet 198

— Qifan

There are many principles that are indeed difficult to understand. The more profound the principle, the more difficult it is to understand. China is the oldest country in the world, and there are especially many profound principles of this kind. Since the business of Western medicine has become increasingly prosperous, and the livelihood of traditional Chinese medicine has become increasingly pressured, the dispute between the new and old medical circles has arisen, a competition for survival. Thus, the name "national medicine" was born. National medicine is of the same nature as national studies. To say that it cannot exist is to say that it does not exist. To argue that it can exist, there are many profound reasons, and it can indeed make people deeply believe in its existence.

Some national doctors also like to use Western medicine, using 606 to treat syphilis, quinine to treat malaria, aspirin for superficial relief, and baking soda for clearing the stomach, etc. But in words, they still maintain their true color as national doctors, talking eloquently about the five elements of mutual generation and overcoming, the roles of monarch, minister, assistant, and guide. That is to say, Chinese learning is the essence, and Western learning is for practical use. What the result is has already been recorded in history.

Later, national doctors realized that their own theories were too profound and difficult for people to understand. So they abandoned their own theories and rose up to attack the lack of depth in Western medical theories. They said that Western doctors only know how to treat headaches by treating the head and foot pain by treating the foot, and there is no fundamental and thorough solution. It must be known that life is a whole, with everything related. The onset of disease has its fundamental cause. By treating the root, it can be cured. This great principle is impeccable and wins the belief of many people. Thus, national medicine is revived, and the call to revive national medicine is raised again.

Some people understand that treating headaches by treating the head and foot pain by treating the foot is not in accordance with medical ethics. So they suddenly realize and say: A headache must be treated by curing the feet. They then follow this method to practice medicine and do things, and implement this principle in all facilities and arrangements. For a time, people's hearts are aroused, and there is a lot of noise. But what the result is, has not yet been seen, because it is still forming historical facts.

More on the Ode to the Ugly Woman 199

— Zizhan

Yesterday, I saw an article submitted to Free Talk by someone with the pen name Yuping. It pointed out that there were slight differences in the wording between the Ode to the Ugly Woman by Liu Sizhen of the Xian Tang Wen edited by Yan Ji, which I quoted, and the one recorded in the Chuxue Ji by Xu Jian. He spared no effort to meticulously proofread it, just like Mr. Hu Linchen's proofreading of my article On Fart Literature. This is even more admirable. However, textual research is difficult, and proofreading is also not easy. Mr. Yuping proofread the Ode to the Ugly Woman only based on the Chuxue Ji, without consulting the Xian Tang Wen edited by Yan Ji, and other Tang and Song encyclopedias such as the Yiwen Leiju and the Taiping Yulan, to compare them one by one. His erudition is still not perfect, so is there any regret? Moreover, after this ode has been proofread and corrected, Mr. Yuping said that all the difficult-to-understand words can be understood, but only the sentence "Zhe e nie lou bi" is still not easy to understand, and he is still afraid that the word "nie" is wrong. From the perspective of someone as ignorant as myself, in what is called understandable, there are still some that I dare not pretend to understand. In what is called not easy to understand, there is also more than one sentence, or at least one word is wrong. Han scholars explained the words "Yue ruo ji gu" in the Shangshu, and they could extend to 100,000 words. Mr. Yuping already has a proofreading addiction or a textual research addiction, why not expand the legacy of Han scholars and annotate this ode with hundreds of thousands of words, so that everyone can understand it? As for Yuping's saying that in the Chuxue Ji, under the Ode to the Ugly Woman, the words "Ci fan bu ju zai" were not noted, as in other articles, and therefore he suspected that it was not a complete piece, it is probably not necessarily so. In fact, Tang and Song encyclopedias often cut, excerpt, revise, and alter, and they never noted them one by one. For example, in the sentence "Zhe e yan lou bi, liang yan xi ru jiu" in the Ode to the Ugly Woman, the Yiwen Leiju writes "Zhe e yan hei mian, lou bi liang yan," which is the original and which is the revised version, who can know? Thank you, Yuping, for your reckless talk. Double the manuscript fee, please eat wine. If wine cannot be eaten, is it necessary for a proofreading expert to change eating to drinking? I have been accumulating boredom for days, and I am laughing about this. Can Mr. Yuping understand my heart?

Pulling 200

— Zhou Muqi

Free Talk has successively pointed out the two phenomena of "pushing" and "kicking". Whether it is pushing or kicking, although the two have different uses depending on the situation and object, the essence and function are still the same.

From pushing and kicking, one can also think of another phenomenon that occurs correspondingly, but the phenomenon itself is the opposite of pushing and kicking, and that is "pulling". This exists not only in our imagination, but also in ordinary facts. For a door or window, there are usually two phenomena of "pushing" and "pulling". If you don't want to use your hand, you can also kick it open with your foot or hook it up. Naturally, crude doors and windows can be kicked or hooked, while luxurious doors and windows can only be pushed or pulled.

It is not enough to have only pushing or kicking. If a door or window is pushed but not pulled, it cannot be pushed again. Although new-style doors and windows can close automatically after being pushed open, this is obviously a reaction to pushing that is similar to pulling. In order to avoid the vibration of this reaction, it is best to pull it in and stop its momentum. To continue pushing, you need to pull it in on one hand. Only by pulling it in can the function of pushing be revealed. The same is true for kicking. Pushing and kicking are opposite and complementary to pulling.

When the Manchus entered China and became the masters, they pulled in the Han literati in order to stabilize their newly acquired privileges of pushing and kicking. Pulling cannot be done unilaterally, and the Han literati naturally also gladly pulled in the newly victorious Manchus in order to maintain their inherent position of pushing and kicking. Who pulled first? That cannot be known. In short, anyone who holds the power to push and kick has the qualification, the possibility, and the necessity to pull.

Ordinary people are not qualified to pull. On the contrary, they have the "share" to be pushed and kicked. This is because "punishment does not extend to officials, and rites do not extend to commoners". If ordinary people could also pull, that would be the "conscription" during military times. Those who are pushed and kicked taste the taste of pulling because of the mutual pushing and kicking of those who push and kick.

During the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom revolution, the Manchus pulled in the Han literati, and the Han literati pulled in Ward and Gordon Baizhiwen, staging a "three-pull reunion". As a result, the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom was kicked down.

Now this comedy is appearing again in the northeast corner. On one end is Japan, which is said to be of the same race and culture, and on the other end are the Manchus and Hans, who have already achieved five races united as one republic. This is the most blatant example.

From the point of view of pulling, the times are reversing, and history is repeating itself.

From "Outside the Great Compassion Temple" to the So-Called Educational Novel 201

— Shiheng

In the August 10th "Free Talk", Mr. Fengwu wrote an article discussing educational novels based on Mr. Lao She's recent work. The term "educational novel" is not only unclear to Mr. Fengwu, but also to many people, because all novels, whether consciously or unconsciously, are doing the work of education. If we say that only novels that depict matters relating to education are educational novels, then the definition is too narrow. But if we say that all novels with a strong educational consciousness can become educational novels, then the definition is too broad. No matter what Mr. Fengwu thinks of this definition, his reasoning using "Outside the Great Compassion Temple" to discuss educational novels is wrong.

Strictly speaking, "Outside the Great Compassion Temple" (originally published in "Literary Monthly", Volume 4, Issue 1) cannot be called an educational novel. Although the material is taken from the relationship between teachers and students in school life, the author's main purpose is to describe two typical people, the first half being that Huang academic supervisor, and the second half being that Ding Geng who beat the academic supervisor to death. Both of them are particularly typical people and cannot represent all academic supervisors and all students. Therefore, the relationship between them is also extremely special. If the author did not write Mr. Huang as an academic supervisor and Ding Geng as a student, the characters and stories could still develop in the same way, because the author did not intend to make them choose these two people and the possibility of this story only exists in school life. Huang academic supervisor is depicted as a personification of "kindness", and Ding Geng is his opposite. Undoubtedly, Mr. Lao She has some aversion to this latter type of person, but in order to make him also reveal a deeper human nature, he applied the old literary trick of conscience condemnation. This kind of writing of course unconsciously exposes the tricks played by the so-called petty bourgeoisie or intellectuals in literature, but the author certainly did not want to use this trick to solve the problem. Even taking a step back, it cannot be said to reflect reality, and is a fabrication of exaggerated facts in order to intentionally make the characters more profound.

Therefore, Mr. Fengwu said, "But is this kind of idealistic self-blame enough to solve the problem? Not at all. Therefore, Ding Geng has no way to save himself, and in education, there is no case where self-condemnation solves disputes." This passage makes people feel that it is somewhat irrelevant.

The author is contradictory in describing the character of Ding Geng. How did he describe Ding Geng at first?｜Look: "At that time, Ding Geng was only seventeen years old. He always wore a small blue cloth shirt, with small red pimples on his face, and his eyes were always a little watery, as if he had applied some eye medicine. He was honest, didn't like to talk, sometimes he was good with you, sometimes he was good with you, sometimes he automatically cleaned up the dormitory, sometimes he didn't wash his face for a day. So he was a young lady｜a little unpredictable." Although this simple and vivid article depicts the character of this young lady vividly, it is inevitably very difficult to transform him into a profound character who is permanently suffering from conscience condemnation. The author only uses a few "never care": "I give in, I never care: "I die, I never care about you": If you want to kill me, please do, I never care", these kinds of words are not enough to be the reason for the transformation of Ding Geng before and after. This kind of contradiction in character is really the shortcoming of this work.

As Mr. Fengwu said, "Only a serious attitude, without a correct creative method, will not receive a powerful effect." However, the so-called "correct creative method" here should not be led to whether conscience condemnation can solve the problem. The "correct creative method" and whether it can actually solve the problem are unrelated.

Therefore, Mr. Fengwu first regarded "Outside the Great Compassion Temple" as an "educational novel" and discussed it, which was already wrong. Secondly, he regarded the conscience condemnation expressed in it as a method of education, which led to the question of whether this doctrine can solve the problem of education, which is even more wrong. Originally, Mr. Fengwu's short article did not need to be pointed out like this, but thinking that the problem committed by this article is exactly the same as the mistake caused by the currently popular idealistic literary theory, and that this method of literary theory is really extremely harmful, I could not help but speak out.

Life and Machine (2) 202

— Sun Yang

Those two skinny black legs became even more tense, and the little bit of muscle left under the dirty skin was full of blood; step up, and then stand on it. Ah, only two steps left, the skinny body suddenly began to sway, like a reed in the wind. The teeth were clenched, and the lonely legs were lifted up again, desperately stepping on the second step. Suddenly, in his chest, a sour and numb thing stirred, rushing upward desperately, rushing into his throat, rushing into his mouth; the eyes turned into a dark mass, the steps, the lights, and his own feet were all gone, only countless small golden dots were flying in the darkness. It sounded like millions of mosquitoes were flying in his ears, buzzing like thunder. His feet suddenly softened, and he fell to the floor of the hold, along with his package, from the side of the unrailed stairs.

"What's wrong? Old Zhang!" A man in old blue cloth pants exclaimed, stopped his feet, and looked down.

"You pig! Haven't you gone back to your hometown yet! Why aren't you moving?" The cursing voice and the whip like a poisonous snake rang again in the noisy and chaotic air.

The man in old blue cloth pants continued to climb up, and the dropped gear teeth were replenished and completed again. A child who had not yet developed, naked, with a piece of greasy and sweaty cloth draped over his shoulders, ran quickly from the iron plate to the stairs, bent down and looked carefully: the old man was lying quietly on his back on the ground, his hands spread out, his legs bent, half of the big package was on his chest, and half was on the ground. In the deep ditch of his chest, fresh blood was flowing lazily. His mouth was slightly open, and a wisp of blood was still hanging on the corner of his mouth. His eyes were open, like a yellow croaker three days out of the water, never blinking.

"How is it? Little Fang." The man in old blue cloth pants walked down the stairs and asked in a low voice. "It's over!" The child wiped the sweat and tears from his forehead with a black cloth, and squeezed out two words from the bottom of his broken heart.

The poisonous curses and the sound of the whip brushing through the air gradually approached them, so the two looked at each other, bit their teeth, and went back to work.

"Snap! Snap!" The whip fell mercilessly on the blood-stained chest, "Hey! Stop pretending to be dead!" There was no expression on the dry face, and even the eyebrows did not move. The big eyes like dried and salted fish turned upward, as if seeing a purpose beyond life. The dry and shriveled mouth was open, and no one's voice would ever come out of it.

A shadow swept across the yellow face on the Xiangyun yarn shirt, and fierce light shot out of the bloodshot eyes; suddenly, that face smiled, and the laughter trembled in the air, like an owl in the deep night, but the greater mixed sound seemed to be buried in this ear-piercing laughter. A hand moved lightly, and the whip drew a big circle in the air, sounding like the string behind a kite in March.

"Black Dog, Little Huang! Roll him up in a reed mat and throw him into the river." The bloodless lips smiled cruelly, and a shadow of sin flashed on the snow-white teeth.

Second

The night wind on the river brought coolness and moisture in gusts, and the pier was immersed in the shadows of the dim electric lights; below, the river was surging, and the waves were flashing with dim light. The large ship was already fully loaded with joy, sorrow, sin, and cargo when it set anchor at dusk.

On the dirty floor of the pier, many tired people were lying like dried salted fish. Under their backs, some used ash-black broken mats, some used broken pieces of cloth, some picked up relatively complete newspapers from the garbage pile and laid them on the ground, and some lay on the rough floor with their backs bare. Everyone's muscles were soft and limp, and their necks were as sore as if they had been hit by a hammer. Those lying on their backs did not have the strength to lie on their sides; those lying on their sides did not want to go to the trouble of turning over. Whatever they were like, they would always be like that, but in this pile of smelly salted fish, there was still a remnant of biological touch, emotion, and fantasy.

Silk and Tea

The Flourishing Hankou Tea Market 210

｜Resurgence of British Tea Merchants in Purchasing｜

Hankou is the gathering place for black tea from the two Hunan and Hubei provinces. In recent years, the amount of tea has greatly decreased due to the devastation of the two provinces by the communist bandits. Furthermore, due to overproduction of tea in India and Ceylon for foreign sales, the British market was unable to promote sales, resulting in the entire Hankou market being manipulated by the Russian aid association. The market was in a state of decline. This year, the communist bandits were mostly eliminated in the tea-producing areas of Hunan and Hubei, and the British tea market also saw a depletion of inventory due to the results of several restrictions on production by British and Dutch tea merchants. Therefore, this year, Indian and Ceylonese tea prices are high, and British tea merchants have no choice but to switch to purchasing Chinese tea. In recent months, the black tea market in the two provinces has been exceptionally prosperous due to the opportunity for British sales to revive. According to statistics, the number of black tea cases loaded and sold by foreign firms is no less than 100,000. Except for 15,000 cases handled by Russian firms, the majority have been purchased entirely by British merchants. Chinese merchants, who have suffered losses for many years, have also benefited slightly, which was quite unexpected by most merchants.

Autumn Silkworms in Hangzhou Approaching Mounting Time

▲Autumn Silkworms in Chang'an Mounting Early as Leaves Thrive: In places like Chang'an, the silkworm season starts earliest. This year, farmers have greatly increased the number of silkworm eggs they are raising. The early batches have already undergone their major molt and the leaves are thriving. There are many silkworms and few leaves, and the price of leaves has already reached two yuan and forty or fifty cents. Mounting will occur shortly.

▲New Silk from Wuxi Factories Transported to Shanghai in Succession: Since the new silk reeling began in Wuxi silk factories, sales of new silk have been sluggish, and inventory has greatly increased. Now, small steamers are offering reduced prices to attract shipments of factory silk. In recent days, small steamers such as Zhaoshang have transported a total of 120 packages of white factory silk.

▲Japanese Artificial Silk Exports Not Weak: Since the price cuts and competitive sales, domestic sales have not been sluggish. Each month, more than 2,000 cases of Japanese artificial silk are transshipped from Shanghai. In the most recent week, the Yanjing and Changjiang Japanese mail steamers have shipped out another 600 cases.

▲No Hope for Turnaround in US Sales of Foreign Silk: There is no possibility of a turnaround in US silk sales in the short term. There is no telegram sent from Shanghai firms. Yesterday, only French firms took the opportunity to replenish missing goods. Xin Fu and others imported twenty packages of white factory silk and twenty packages of yellow factory silk. Prices remained weak.

Page 21

Talks

Birth 211

— Cunren

A child is born, not knowing what he is to do in this world, nor whether his life will be happy or painful. He is simply here and must live on. If he knew that the road of life is not easy to walk, I think he would immediately starve himself to death. However, his parents, especially his mother, cherish him even more than they cherish themselves. Although they have some hopes for him, they don't necessarily have specific expectations for his future. People often hold a kind of commemorative ceremony for their birthday, which is said to have two meanings: one is to commemorate the nurturing grace of parents, and the other is to celebrate one's own survival. In this day and age, when we poor people encounter our birthday, I think it will instead arouse feelings of resentment. It is difficult to survive, and it is even more difficult to be a person. Even the day of birth is like the year of death. Survival is like a chicken rib, so what is there to celebrate or commemorate on a birthday? However, a certain great writer, because he escaped smallpox, said, "It is truly a blessing from heaven, and it would not be excessive to hold a celebration every year." There is another kind of brilliant insight regarding the meaning of birthday commemoration, which is that if one is "blessed by heaven," it would be concerning not to commemorate and celebrate. This kind of brilliant insight is certainly admirable, but it is only felt by those who are "blessed by heaven." People who are "blessed by heaven" are afraid of being kidnapped by bandits and worried about being robbed. They live in fear and trepidation throughout the year. Fortunately, with the blessing of the heavens, another year has easily passed to their birthday, so naturally, they must celebrate it greatly. What about us poor people? We have nothing to our name, and our two hands are our capital. Those who are employed fear losing their jobs, and those who are unemployed suffer from hunger and cold. Living a life on the edge, what is there to celebrate? However, we must also say that "Heaven has the virtue of cherishing life." Seeking to live is human nature, and being poor but strong is indeed something to celebrate. The rich can celebrate their birthdays, so why can't the poor eat longevity noodles?

Sacrificing for Religion 212

— Wei

Laborers who toil all day long in this deformed society feel that their lives should not be as mechanically dull, monotonous, and burdensome. They feel that they should have a kind of life force, a "vita," to regulate their exhausted bodies and gain some pleasure, or to get some spiritual nourishment and reduce some physical pain. So they are desperately pursuing it.

But what are they supposed to pursue? They often run into walls in bad environments. So they become passive and degenerate. Recently, a news item was discovered in the newspaper: a sixteen-year-old apprentice sacrificed himself for religion. This is a young man who ran from passivity into the path of blindness.

First, we must know that the young man who committed suicide was an apprentice in a store. Is the life of an apprentice interesting? Of course not. But he knew that he wanted to pursue some pleasure, but an apprentice and his environment cannot allow you to develop freely. So he still ran into the idealistic and hopeful group of religion. In addition, those missionaries desperately put on a compassionate face of saving people from suffering to invite them to the great path of their savior, especially working hard for a group of people who labor during the day, because that group of laboring people urgently needs a kind of spiritual nourishment. People without much education and thought feel that there is no way out of reality, so they are particularly enthusiastic in the religious faith. In religious belief, they are told to put aside the present and yearn for the future. I remember a poem:

Hundreds of millions of beings, be bold and endure:

For there is a better world to reward you! Originally, religion only gave him "unreachable grapes," so he committed suicide by borrowing the motive of the torn holy book.

Whose fault is this?

Finally, I still hope to follow Mr. Cai Yuanpei's words: "Let art replace religion" and pull the great number of masses out of anesthesia and onto a new path!

He Went to Mourn Chen Rui at her House Before

The Proliferation of Schools 213

— Yin

｜Is it Progress? Or Decline?｜

Whenever we talk about any issue, whenever we are disappointed, and whenever we are at a loss for words, we all say: "This is due to the lack of widespread education. The only reliable remedy for the lack of public knowledge is to establish schools and popularize education." I walk the long, snaking XX Road every day. Although the fine sand on the road is blown away by the wind, my footprints have long since disappeared. Because I walk it every day, I am particularly familiar with everything on XX Road. What particularly catches my eye and awakens me is XX Public School, XX Middle School, XX Elementary School... etc. Some even have the grand and impressive inscription "Registered with the Municipal Bureau of Education" or "Approved by the Municipal Bureau of Education" above the school name. Ah! This is clearly a very "scenic" phenomenon. There are so many schools on XX Road. Ah! The proliferation of schools is quite a spectacle!

Because I am also a member of one of these schools, I pay particular attention to these things unintentionally. There are too many schools. Our school will be affected! If I have one less student, wouldn't that mean a few yuan less in tuition fees? Misfortune!

One day, feeling very bored, I went with a colleague to visit many of the nearby schools. There, one or two reception rooms no more than ten feet square were filled with a few desks that were barely shaped like desks and a small square blackboard. That was all. This kind of simplicity is what is called a "school," so it is no wonder that "schools" are proliferating. I could only sigh as I left.

This is completely a vestige or transformation of private schools. The fundamental difference is that instead of sitting and dozing off, there are now classes, breaks, and recesses. Instead of blindly reciting "Zhao Qian Sun Li...", it has changed to "yours," "mine," "dog," "cat," but what other beneficial improvements are there? Yes, the textbooks are too simple. Therefore, even those who know only three and a half characters can teach. The rate of unemployment in society has inflated at a high speed, so, due to the straits of livelihood, they have no choice but to use these "schools" as temporary shelters.

The most ridiculous thing is that I saw the following sentence on the badge of a certain school: "If siblings come together, tuition fees can be discounted by 5%." Ha! Thank you very much. The enthusiasm of the organizers of education, the unreserved promotion of the grand meaning of education, and the caring for the poor compatriots. There is also a certain school that even drew a "genuine" complete map of the school buildings in its recruitment advertisement - because they are so-called foreign-style houses! Ah! The predicament of the organizers of education. They want to use the school buildings to attract a general group of vain elementary school students and arouse their interest in studying. This is truly what is called "meticulousness."

In short, schools are proliferating on XX Road. "Is this phenomenon scenic? Is it strange? Is it progress or decline?" I think so!

Clerk Correspondence

Harming Oneself 214

Editor:

I am very grateful to you for answering my previous letter in your column. Now I have another unexpected problem to trouble you with. Please understand my difficulties. The matter of the missing money has not yet been resolved, and then there was a theft of more than a dozen five-cent postage stamps. Although it is a small matter, the suspicion is even more serious than before. I thought that a dozen stamps would not be used up in a short time, so that night, I secretly and carefully searched for them. Later, I found them in a colleague's drawer (where he puts books and other items). The next day, I publicly stated everything that had happened. He, in order to deny what he had done, had no choice but to use a trick, claiming that others had framed him. Everyone also asked in unison whether there was a second witness when the stamps were found. Ah! This was a clue found in secret, so of course there was no second witness. Sir, isn't this like lifting a stone only to drop it on one's own foot? I really have no way to defend myself. Otherwise, would such a small matter be likely to be brought to court? Sir, could you answer me with a better solution?

I would rather sacrifice other things than lose my reputation. I am now waiting for your good news! Sincerely yours, Gu Yueyi

Editor's Note: Previously, Mr. Gu wrote to us asking for advice because he was suspected of stealing money from the store. Our answer was to tell you to secretly pay attention: people who are used to doing business without capital (thieves) will definitely not stop there. You only need to catch them the second time, and the truth will be revealed. Now, as we expected, the second theft has been discovered. The reason why you have ended up harming yourself is entirely because your procedures were not precise. Lifting a stone and ending up hurting your own foot is entirely because you are weak or did not lift it properly. If you were strong enough, how could you harm yourself? If, after finding the stamps, you had not immediately reported it publicly, but had observed him with a cold eye, and then caught him after he used the stamps, how could he have blamed it on others?

So this time our answer is still the same as before. Fortunately, they only have suspicion of you, and there is no more serious situation that forces you to seek a quick resolution. In the future, if you encounter an opportunity, you should pay special attention to the procedures to avoid being bitten back. Litigation is unnecessary, and indeed unnecessary.

Novel

War and Peace (III) 215

— Ling He

Old Woman: Yes! What can you do when you encounter such a thing? Unfortunately, my second child was taken away by the enemy to carry bullets, and it has been more than twenty days now, and he has not returned. Who knows if he is even alive? My second daughter-in-law cries at home hating heaven and earth all day long. Her poor eyes are swollen from crying, but what's the use?

Middle-aged Man C: But thinking about it again and again, since it is for the sake of the country, there is no way to blame anyone. As long as we can repel the enemy and recover the three northeastern provinces, even if we become beggars, it is better than being a subjugated people. What do a few head of livestock matter?

Middle-aged Man: But then again, haven't we already paid our grain and taxes? As the saying goes, "Raising soldiers for a thousand days, using them for one morning." Now that we have fought a battle with Japan, we are again asking our common people to carry guns and horses. Isn't that too much?

Middle-aged Man B: Of course. The civil war already left us destitute and ruined. Now that we are fighting foreigners, it will inevitably take our lives even more.

Old Woman: It's strange, even the bodhisattvas are not working in these times. During the first month, I drew a fortune stick in this temple. It said that we had to wait until the Yellow Bull Mountain produced the True Son of Heaven in the third month for the world to have peace. But it has been so long now, and the Son of Heaven should have been born long ago, but there is still no peace. Who knows what's going on?

Middle-aged Man B: The bodhisattvas are never reliable.

Old Man: You can't say that. Hasn't the True Son of Heaven in Jinan Prefecture, Shandong, already created the divine bull carriage? But the time hasn't come yet. We still have to suffer a little more. Perhaps the Jade Emperor wants us to suffer more so that he can see if the beings in the lower realm will repent. For example, last year's Water and Land Dharma Assembly in Beijing could have liberated all beings, but the people were not taught to be pure, abstain from slaughter, and fast, so not only did it not move the gods, but it angered the Jade Emperor, who sent the god of slaughter to descend and kill a hundred thousand eight thousand. Who knows if the head of this village is not the reincarnation of the god of slaughter? In short, China's destiny has come to an end. The will of Heaven is so, and there is no way to change it.

Child: Then hasn't Emperor Puyi already ascended the throne? Why are we still fighting here and there?

Middle-aged Man C: You are just a child. What do you know? It is precisely because he has ascended the throne that he has to fight for the world.

Middle-aged Man A: You can't say that. This time, we fought past the Great Wall, but it's not because Puyi wants to fight. It's the Japanese who came up with the idea. Puyi is just a puppet.

Old Woman: I heard that this Emperor Puyi is still very young.

Old Man: That's right. He's the same age as my youngest child, born in the year of the horse. He's only twenty-eight years old this year. So, if fate has determined that he is to be an emperor, he will always be an emperor. But this kind of emperor cannot be relied on.
